## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping/driving (functions of v), and possibly explicit time-dependent forcing. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v * x**2 (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (regularized dry friction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial in x for symmetric potentials
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x²·v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators (van der Pol type)
- Explicit sinusoidal time dependence sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) indicates externally driven/forced oscillation
- If acceleration depends only on x (not t or v), the system is conservative and energy-preserving — look for pure polynomial in x
- Linear v terms represent viscous damping (energy dissipation rate proportional to velocity)
- Even powers of x in restoring force (x²) break spatial symmetry — indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Products of time-periodic functions with x (e.g., x·cos(c·t)) indicate parametric excitation rather than direct forcing
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient on v) combined with cubic velocity term (v³) indicates limit cycle behavior
- Phase-space structure: if dv_dt = f(x, v) with no explicit t, the system is autonomous and trajectories don't cross in (x,v) space
